      </a><!----><!----> <!----></div> <div class="tw-mt-2.5 tw-flex tw-flex-wrap tw-items-center tw-text-sm !tw-mt-0"><!----> <div><!----> <!----></div> <div class="tw-relative tw-ml-5 tw-flex tw-items-center before:tw-absolute before:tw-top-0 before:tw-bottom-0 before:tw--left-3 before:tw-m-auto before:tw-block before:tw-h-1 before:tw-w-1 before:tw-rounded-full before:tw-bg-[#7c7c7c] sm:first:before:tw-hidden"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="14" height="14" viewBox="0 0 23 23" overflow="visible" class="tw-text-[#7c7c7c]"><path d="M11.5 2c5.2 0 9.5 4.3 9.5 9.5S16.7 21 11.5 21 2 16.7 2 11.5 6.3 2 11.5 2m0-2C5.1 0 0 5.1 0 11.5S5.1 23 11.5 23 23 17.9 23 11.5 17.9 0 11.5 0z" style="fill: currentColor"></path> <path d="M11.5 6.6v4.5M12 12.1l3.5 3.2" class="st0"></path></svg> <span class="tw-pl-2">
            11 min read
         </span></div> <div class="tw-relative tw-ml-5 before:tw-absolute before:tw-top-0 before:tw-bottom-0 before:tw--left-3 before:tw-m-auto before:tw-block before:tw-h-1 before:tw-w-1 before:tw-rounded-full before:tw-bg-[#7c7c7c]"><button aria-label="add to bookmark" class="tw-block tw-text-base"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="20" viewBox="0 0 50.9 52.1" overflow="visible" class="tw-w-[1em] tw-h-[1em]"><path d="M3.4 2.5h34.3c.4 0 .7.4.7.8v45.2c0 .6-.6.9-.9.5L21.1 37.3c-.4-.3-.8-.3-1.2 0L3.4 49.5c-.4.4-.9.1-.9-.5l.2-45.7c0-.4.3-.8.7-.8z" fill="#fff" stroke="#adb5b9" stroke-width="5" stroke-miterlimit="10"></path></svg> <!----></button></div></div></div> <h1 class="tw-text-3xl tw-font-bold md:tw-text-4xl md:tw-leading-tight xl:tw-text-5xl xl:tw-leading-tight">
               Stream-Jacking 2.0: Deep fakes power account takeovers on YouTube to maximize crypto-doubling scams
            </h1> <div class="tw-mt-3 tw-items-center tw-text-sm sm:tw-flex"><div class="sm:tw-w-1/3"><div class="tw-mt-2.5 tw-flex tw-flex-wrap tw-items-center tw-text-sm"><a href="/en-gb/blog/labs/author/ionut-baltariu/" title="Ionut Alexandru BALTARIU" class="tw-overflow-hidden tw-rounded-full tw-h-11 tw-w-11"><img width="50" height="50" alt="Ionut Alexandru BALTARIU" title="Ionut Alexandru BALTARIU" data-src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w100/2023/10/BSP_3250.jpg" class="tw-h-full tw-w-full tw-object-cover"></a><a href="/en-gb/blog/labs/author/emanuel-puscasu/" title="Emanuel PUSCASU" class="tw-overflow-hidden tw-rounded-full tw-h-11 tw-w-11"><img width="50" height="50" alt="Emanuel PUSCASU" title="Emanuel PUSCASU" data-src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w100/2023/10/1631980503114.jpg" class="tw-h-full tw-w-full tw-object-cover"></a> <div class="tw-pl-2"><div><a href="/en-gb/blog/labs/author/ionut-baltariu/" title="Ionut Alexandru BALTARIU" class="tw-mr-1.5 last:tw-mr-0">Ionut Alexandru BALTARIU
         </a><a href="/en-gb/blog/labs/author/emanuel-puscasu/" title="Emanuel PUSCASU" class="tw-mr-1.5 last:tw-mr-0">Emanuel PUSCASU
         </a></div> <p class="tw-text-[#41485e]">
         January 18, 2024
      </p></div> <!----> <!----></div></div> <div class="tw-mt-4 sm:tw-mt-0 sm:tw-w-2/3"><div class="tw-relative tw-rounded tw-bg-[#f4f7fa] tw-py-2 tw-pl-11 tw-pr-2 tw-text-xs"><em class="tw-absolute tw-left-2.5 tw-top-2 tw-text-[10px]">Promo</em> <span class="pe-2">Protect all your devices, without slowing them down.</span> <br> <a target="_blank" href="/Downloads/" class="tw-text-[#608dff]">Free 30-day trial</a></div></div></div> <picture class="tw-my-6"><source data-not-lazy="" media="(max-width: 600px)" data-srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/ai-deepfake.jpg"> <source data-not-lazy="" media="(min-width: 701px)" data-srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w1000/2024/01/ai-deepfake.jpg"> <img data-not-lazy="" data-src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/ai-deepfake.jpg" alt="Stream-Jacking 2.0: Deep fakes power account takeovers on YouTube to maximize crypto-doubling scams" title="Stream-Jacking 2.0: Deep fakes power account takeovers on YouTube to maximize crypto-doubling scams" width="600" height="400" src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/ai-deepfake.jpg" class="tw-my-4 tw-w-full"></picture> <div class="content tw-mb-12 tw-text-lg tw-text-black"><p>As of October 2023, researchers at Bitdefender Labs have been actively <a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/blog/labs/a-deep-dive-into-stream-jacking-attacks-on-youtube-and-why-theyre-so-popular/">keeping tabs</a> on steam-jacking attacks against high-profile YouTube accounts used to conduct a myriad of crypto doubling scams.</p><p>Fast forward to 2024; our investigation into the fraudulent takeovers and usage of YouTube accounts has rendered new findings, as financially motivated threat actors meticulously evolve their attacks.</p><p>Over the past couple of months, stream-jacking attacks have steadily evolved, and our research shows how cybercriminals advance their craft to maximize the reach and efficiency of their actions with carefully engineered content that closely mimics legitimate cryptocurrency-related news or announcements.</p><p>We know that malicious actors often stay on top of popular events in Crypto, and during the last quarter they have made use of multiple announcements to potentially monetize fraudulent livestreams that disguise crypto-doubling scams under popular titles highlighted in mainstream media.</p><p>For example, attackers made use of the “SpaceX Starship integrated flight test 2” official event to launch their own fake livestreams under the name <em>SpaceX Launch Starship Flight Test! Elon Musk gives update on Starship! </em>on ‘verified’ compromised channels to add credibility to their ruse. Most of the livestreams we analyzed were also showing signs of artificial boosting of viewers to further increase the trust of potential real viewers.</p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/image--7-.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="895" height="528" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/image--7-.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/image--7-.png 895w" sizes="(min-width: 720px) 720px"></figure><p>As previously stated, scammers use variants of the name of the impersonated entity on compromised accounts (instead of @SpaceX, @spacex1[..] is observed in the example above).</p><p>Other premeditated scams based on official and wide-known events we have found are the following:</p><p><strong>1.    </strong> <strong>Nov. 30 was an important date for the SEC-XRP trial in the world of cryptocurrencies.</strong> Before, during and after that date, we noticed multiple fake livestreams with the following titles:</p><p>o   Ripple XRP Case Reaching A HAPPY End - SEC Lose? Brad Garlinghouse LIVE;</p><p>o   Ripple XRP BOOM! Case Reaching A HAPPY End - SEC Lose? Brad Garlinghouse LIVE</p><p>o   Tomorrow Swell will send XRP? Brad Garlinghouse LIVE!</p><p><strong>2.     The USSF-52 flight</strong></p><p>o   SpaceX USSF-52 Mission Launch! Elon Musk gives update on Starship!</p><p>o   USSF-52 Mission Launch SpaceX! Elon Musk gives update on Starship!</p><p><strong>3.     Changpeng Zhao stepping down from the CEO position of Binance</strong></p><p>o   Changpeng Zhao: I'm not leaving! I'm free! Today is a big event! Scan the QR code and read the rules</p><p>o   Bitcoin | BTC news today | ETH price prediction 2024 | Crypto news | ETH moon | Ethereum pump x2 🚀,Changpeng-Zhao LIVE</p><p>o   Elon Musk: BNB (Binance) CRASH TOMORROW, 21.11.2023",Binance Live</p><p><strong>4.     The Cybertruck Launch</strong></p><p>o   Elon Musk Live: Tesla's Cybertruck Debut and Production Insights!</p><p>o   REVOLUTION: Tesla Van &amp; Minivan - a van that combines Model 3, Model X &amp; Model Y</p><p><strong>5.  </strong>   <strong>Bitcoin ETF</strong>:</p><p>o   Bitcoin ETF Will Send BTC Price to $1 Million? Michael Saylor LIVE</p><p>o   Michael Saylor: MicroStrategy Buys Another 16,000 Bitcoin. This is Why Bull Run is INEVITABLE</p><p>o   Ripple ETF Will Send XRP Price to $40? Brad Garlinghouse LIVE</p><p>o   Elon Musk: Bitcoin ETF Will Send BTC Price to $1 Million? Tesla LIVE</p><p>o   Bitcoin Is About To 100X  - Michael Saylor's Genius BTC Strategy!</p><p>o   Michael Saylor: Why Will Bitcoin Cost $200k?! Is Ethereum Expecting A Pump?! X100 BTC&amp;ETH</p><p>o   Michael Saylor - ACCEPTED Bitcoin ETF today! What will happen to BTC in the near future?</p><p>o   Bitcoin ETF APPROVED!! Bitcoin $1 Million tomorrow! Michael Saylor LIVE</p><p>It becomes more obvious that any high-profile news headlines can be used in malicious activities. Over time, the scams evolved from the simple use of the names of famous entities to the coordination of scam campaigns based on real events of interest to online communities.</p><p>More importantly, we’ve noticed that at the start of these planned campaigns, a considerable number of the compromised channels have many subscribers (some with more than 1 million and one with as much as 12.5 million) which makes them an ideal vector for threat actors to spread their fraudulent schemes.</p><p><strong>The rise of deep fakes reshapes the threat landscape</strong></p><p>While the initial iterations of the scams reported in October 2023 used looped videos of famous conference talks or other popular recordings, fraudsters have recently started using deep fake technology to create fake videos of prominent figures in cryptocurrency and adding further credibility to the scams.</p><p>A common aspect of these skillfully engineered videos is that they encourage viewers to look for a QR code, scan it and send an amount of crypto to be doubled.</p><p>Some of the observed deep fakes are of decent quality and could easily fool an untrained eye. To prevent any victims or wary community members from blowing the lid on the entire operation, the live chat section of the videos is disabled unless you are a selected member of the channel or have been a subscriber for an extended period.</p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Picture1.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="319" height="246"></figure><p></p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Picture2.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="268" height="480"></figure><p>Another new commonality of these deepfakes is that they are sometimes used in YouTube ads instead of malicious livestreams, giving cybercriminals more leeway for spreading the scams (fraudsters can easily pay for these phony ads until they are banned by YouTube).</p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-28-194443.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="1286" height="828" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-28-194443.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w1000/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-28-194443.png 1000w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-28-194443.png 1286w" sizes="(min-width: 720px) 720px"></figure><p>An example of a malicious stream that was also preceded by a malicious ad</p><p>While the videos are clearly crafted with deep generative models, the support chats that the malicious websites use do not seem to employ any Large Language Model to answer.</p><h3 id="the-anatomy-of-youtube-account-takeovers">The anatomy of YouTube account takeovers</h3><p></p><p>These account takeovers are usually enabled by the compromise of YouTube access tokens with the use of various stealers. After the access tokens are obtained, the malicious actors proceed with revamping the channel, making it look like it is owned by the entity they want to impersonate. This process is most likely automated and consists of completely changing the original channel by:</p><ul><li> Changing the channel name and handle – even though these are operations that can be done twice every 14 days, hackers manage to do it as it is uncommon for content creators to change names that often;</li><li>Changing the visibility of all videos to <strong>private – </strong>this is done to conceal previously existing content as it can directly lead to the discovery of the scam;</li><li>Changing the channel avatar and banner – these are replaced with images that represent the impersonated entity;</li><li>Changing or eliminating the channel’s description, links, featured channels and anything that might lead to the identification of the original channel. In some instances, the channel link is set to the malicious website that promotes the crypto doubling scam.</li></ul><p>In our research, we’ve observed some takeovers live. An example of this can be seen below.</p><p>The name, handle and avatar of the original channel were changed, but previously existing content is still available despite the start of the malicious broadcast:</p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-20-225106-1.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="1330" height="875" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-20-225106-1.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w1000/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-20-225106-1.png 1000w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-20-225106-1.png 1330w" sizes="(min-width: 720px) 720px"></figure><p>After a couple of minutes, videos were set to private and the banner was also changed, but the channel description and special videos are still displayed:</p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/takeover_after_Some_mins-2.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="1177" height="793" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/takeover_after_Some_mins-2.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w1000/2024/01/takeover_after_Some_mins-2.png 1000w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/takeover_after_Some_mins-2.png 1177w" sizes="(min-width: 720px) 720px"></figure><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="blob:https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/1248cfa3-dffa-4cd4-90c4-ccb3d4396ca2" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy"></figure><p>After another couple of minutes, the channel is completely stripped of the original content:</p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/takeover_after_Some_mins_2.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="1140" height="681" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/takeover_after_Some_mins_2.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w1000/2024/01/takeover_after_Some_mins_2.png 1000w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/takeover_after_Some_mins_2.png 1140w" sizes="(min-width: 720px) 720px"></figure><p></p><p>In this case, the definitive version of the compromised channel scarcely looks like the official SpaceX channel:</p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Picture3.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="563" height="197"></figure><p>Sometimes, these transformative operations either take too much to happen (and the channel gets banned before it does) or do not happen at all.</p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-24-193657.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="1066" height="849" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-24-193657.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w1000/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-24-193657.png 1000w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-24-193657.png 1066w" sizes="(min-width: 720px) 720px"></figure><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-28-195622.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="1294" height="767" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-28-195622.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w1000/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-28-195622.png 1000w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Screenshot-2023-11-28-195622.png 1294w" sizes="(min-width: 720px) 720px"></figure><p></p><p><strong>The last wave of scams: MicroStrategy and the Bitcoin ETF</strong></p><p>Taking advantage of the heavy news coverage of the Bitcoin ETF, malicious actors started broadcasting scams with the same topic in late December 2023. These scams have MicroStrategy (business intelligence company) and Michael Saylor as central figures, and use titles that refer to the Bitcoin ETF potentially reaching high values to gain traction. Hundreds of malicious broadcasts were observed in the last couple of weeks, qualifying it as one of the most intensive scam campaigns we’ve seen so far.</p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/saylor_campaign.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="828" height="843" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/saylor_campaign.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/saylor_campaign.png 828w" sizes="(min-width: 720px) 720px"></figure><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Screenshot-2024-01-06-170150.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="1533" height="829" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/Screenshot-2024-01-06-170150.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w1000/2024/01/Screenshot-2024-01-06-170150.png 1000w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Screenshot-2024-01-06-170150.png 1533w" sizes="(min-width: 720px) 720px"></figure><p></p><p>Most of the broadcasts use looped deep fakes in which MicroStrategy’s former CEO encourages the community to “participate in the giveaway” by scanning the QR code and following the instructions found on the website.</p><p>The compromised channels use variations of the official MicroStrategy logo as the avatar and the official banner, and some refer to the playlists of the official MicroStrategy channel to boost credibility. The thumbnails of the videos are also common between instances, with limited diversity. The most common name after the takeover is <strong>MicroStrategy US</strong> and other discovered names are: MicroStrategy, Microstrategy, Microstrategy US, Microstrategy Live, Micro Strategy. The names might include trailing spaces and parentheses (rounded or square) around the <strong>US </strong>and <strong>Live</strong> keywords.</p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Picture7.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="336" height="59"></figure><p>The phony websites are usually hosted on domains that resemble the name of the impersonated company or its former CEO, or simpler domains that include the symbols of the cryptocurrencies used in the fake giveaways, along with multipliers such as <em>2x </em>or <em>x2</em>. These websites also host animations that give users the impression that multiple transactions are taking place live. While it may seem legitimate, these are in fact randomly generated.</p><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Picture4.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="480" height="415"></figure><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/crypto.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="912" height="186" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/crypto.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/crypto.png 912w" sizes="(min-width: 720px) 720px"></figure><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Picture5-1.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="1477" height="726" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/Picture5-1.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w1000/2024/01/Picture5-1.png 1000w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Picture5-1.png 1477w" sizes="(min-width: 720px) 720px"></figure><figure class="kg-card kg-image-card"><img src="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Picture6-1.png" class="kg-image" alt loading="lazy" width="640" height="312" srcset="https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/size/w600/2024/01/Picture6-1.png 600w, https://blogapp.bitdefender.com/labs/content/images/2024/01/Picture6-1.png 640w"></figure><p>Here are some key insights about what the deepfake Michael Saylor tells viewers in the looped video:</p><p>-       You don’t need to register on any website. You need to watch the live broadcast online, keep an eye out for the QR code that will appear on the screen and scan it with your phone.</p><p>-       You don’t need to register on the website to make a Bitcoin deposit. Once you’ve accessed the platform, you’ll be prompted to deposit any amount of Bitcoin.</p><p>-       After you deposit, our system will automatically send back double the amount of Bitcoin you deposited.</p><p>-       We’ve ensured that the entire process is smooth and hassle-free to those who are new to the world of cryptocurrencies.</p><p>-       Our technical support team will be available during the broadcast to assist with any queries or guidance</p><p>-       Unlike traditional giveaways that rely on chance, our mode is based on a guaranteed outcome. When participants deposit Bitcoin, they automatically receive double.</p><p>-       The sooner you participate, the better your chance is, as the offer is time sensitive and depends on the availability of the funds allocated for the giveaway.</p><p><strong>Updated numbers on the phenomenon</strong></p><p>·      Maximum number of subscribers of a hijacked account: ~12,500,000 (for one account)</p><p>·      Maximum number of views of a hijacked account:  ~3,869,224,308 (total views/one channel)</p><p>·      Subscribers count median value: ~3955</p><p>·      View count of channel median value: ~449,159</p><p>·      Total number of subscribers from the top 10 hijacked channels: ~62,930,000</p><p>·      Total number of views from the most viewed 10 hijacked channels: ~17,447,370,155</p><p>·      According to our analysis, cybercriminals targeted a variety of content creator accounts, including the US (96 accounts), Brazil (75 accounts), India (74 accounts), Indonesia (49 accounts), Mexico (21 accounts), Turkey (15 accounts), Peru (14 accounts), Vietnam (13 accounts), Columbia (12 accounts), the UK (11 accounts), France (9 accounts), Spain (8 accounts, and much more. The number of compromised accounts does not include any accounts already banned by YouTube following malicious/fraudulent broadcasts</p><p>All metrics have grown since our last <a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/blog/labs/a-deep-dive-into-stream-jacking-attacks-on-youtube-and-why-theyre-so-popular/">report</a> on the topic, while some even come close to doubling. The alarming growth indicates that this phenomenon is far from eradicated.</p><p><strong>Top 10 most subscribed hijacked channels</strong><br><br></p><!--kg-card-begin: html--><table class="MsoTableGrid" border="1" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="caret-color: rgb(0, 0, 0); As such, we began an investigation of a subset of malicious domains (focusing on the latest trends – XRP, MicroStrategy, SpaceX and Binance) that were promoted in livestreams to get an idea of the actual “profits.” After extracting the identifiers of the promoted crypto wallets, the associated transactions were analyzed, with the following insights:</p><p>·      Over 10 ETH (Ethereum, having a value per coin between ~$2180 and ~$2690 since January 1,<sup>,</sup>2024) and 12 BTC (Bitcoin, having a value per coin between ~$42,200 and ~$48,700 since January 1, 2024) were sent to the malicious wallets;</p><p>·      Most of the wallets had no transactions. This can also be related to the fact that their date of creation is quite recent, so it is likely that the numbers will grow in the future;</p><p>·      Hackers use well-known measures of passing the tokens through a series of other wallets to complicate future analyses;</p><p>·      The highest amounts received are almost 6 BTC and 2 ETH.</p><p>In total, potential earnings amount to ~$528,200 and ~$600,500 (depending on what date the coins are evaluated), making these malicious operations highly profitable for threat actors. While the analysis solely relies on the transactions received, it is unclear if these transactions are from the actual victims or transactions from other wallets used in this kind of scam. Nonetheless, the numbers are alarming, and the need to raise awareness of such frauds is paramount.</p><p><strong>Fighting fire with fire. How Bitdefender’s AI-powered scam detector can help keep users safe from deepfake crypto scams and more</strong></p><p>While cybercriminals continue to use technological advancements and AI to create more legitimate-looking messages and videos to defraud internet users, steal personal data and take over their digital lives, we’re working to level the playing field.</p><p>Bitdefender Scamio, powered by leading-edge AI and Bitdefender threat protection and detection technologies, acts as a personal scam detection chatbot that can help you defend against fraud attempts you come by via emails, texts, links and even QR codes that may pop up in cryptocurrency livestreams that promise huge returns on investment.</p><p>Bitdefender Scamio is extremely easy to use and can be accessed via web browser or Facebook Messenger following the quick setup of a Bitdefender account. It’s completely free and can help individuals immediately counter fraud attempts.</p><p>Good cyber-hygiene and vigilance can also boost your online safety. We recommend installing a security solution and always inspecting videos with click-bait messages that encourage immediate Bitcoin deposits for double or triple returns and never scanning QR codes you see in videos or ads promoting cryptocurrency giveaways.</p><p>You can read more about how to keep YouTube accounts safe from hijackers and preventing crypto doubling scams in our dedicated <a href="https://www.bitdefender.com/blog/labs/a-deep-dive-into-stream-jacking-attacks-on-youtube-and-why-theyre-so-popular/">guide</a>.</p><p>If you ever observe content promoting giveaways or other events from well-known companies, always make sure to double-check the promotions on official websites. The ones discussed in the present material are the following:</p><p>·      <a href="https://www.microstrategy.com/">https://www.microstrategy.com/</a></p><p>·      <a href="https://binance.com/">https://binance.com/</a></p><p>·      <a href="https://www.spacex.com/">https://www.spacex.com/</a></p><p>·      <a href="https://ripple.com/">https://ripple.com/</a></p><p>·      <a href="https://www.tesla.com/">https://www.tesla.com/</a></p><p>And the associated YouTube channels:</p><p>·      <a href="https://www.youtube.com/@microstrategy">https://www.youtube.com/@microstrategy</a></p><p>·      <a href="https://www.youtube.com/@BinanceYoutube">https://www.youtube.com/@BinanceYoutube</a></p><p>·      <a href="https://www.youtube.com/@SpaceX">https://www.youtube.com/@SpaceX</a></p><p>·      <a href="https://www.youtube.com/@Ripple">https://www.youtube.com/@Ripple</a></p><p>·      <a href="https://www.youtube.com/@tesla">https://www.youtube.com/@tesla</a></p><p>Always keep an eye out for the identifier of the channel – if it contains unexpected characters or misspellings, it is almost certain that it is the case of an impersonation. Always <a href="https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/2802027">report</a> observed scams to aid in keeping the phenomenon under control. Also, keep an eye on various social media feeds, as these scams are usually denounced and detailed there – for example, Twitter/X <a href="https://twitter.com/search?q=microstrategy%20scam">posts</a> about the MicroStrategy YouTube scams are common.</p></div> <div><!----> <div><p class="tw-py-4 tw-pl-4 tw-font-bold tw-uppercase">tags</p></div> <!----></div> <div class="tw-mb-2.5 tw-flex tw-flex-wrap tw-items-center tw-text-xs tw-font-bold tw-uppercase tw-text-[#608DFF]"><a href="/en-gb/blog/labs/tag/antimalware-research/" title="Anti-Malware Research" class="tw-mr-4 tw-mb-4 tw-border tw-border-[#eff0f1] tw-bg-white tw-p-4 tw-text-xs tw-font-normal tw-lowercase tw-text-[#7c7c7c] hover:tw-bg-[#d4d7d9]">Anti-Malware Research

fraudulent takeovers and usage of YouTube accounts has rendered new findings, as financially motivated threat actors meticulously evolve their attacks.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EOver the past couple of months, stream-jacking attacks have steadily evolved, and our research shows how cybercriminals advance their craft to maximize the reach and efficiency of their actions with carefully Michael Saylor LIVE\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIt becomes more obvious that any high-profile news headlines can be used in malicious activities. Over time, the scams evolved from the simple use of the names of famous entities to the coordination of scam campaigns based on real events of interest to online communities.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EMore importantly, we’ve noticed that at the start of these planned campaigns, a considerable number of the compromised channels have many subscribers (some with more than 1 million and one with as much as 12.5 million) which makes them an ideal vector for threat actors to spread their fraudulent schemes.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe rise of deep fakes reshapes the threat landscape\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhile the initial iterations of the scams reported in October 2023 used looped videos of famous conference talks or other popular recordings, fraudsters have recently started using deep fake technology to create fake videos of prominent figures in cryptocurrency and adding further credibility to the scams.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EA common aspect of these skillfully engineered videos is that they encourage viewers to look for a QR code, scan it and send an amount of crypto to be doubled.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESome of the observed deep fakes are of decent quality and could easily fool an untrained eye. To prevent any victims or wary community members from blowing the lid on the entire operation, the live chat section of the videos is disabled unless you are a selected member of the channel or have been a subscriber for an extended period.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F01\u002FPicture1.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"319\" height=\"246\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F01\u002FPicture2.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"268\" height=\"480\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAnother new commonality of these deepfakes is that they are sometimes used in YouTube ads instead of malicious livestreams, giving cybercriminals more leeway for spreading the scams (fraudsters can easily pay for these phony ads until they are banned by YouTube).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F01\u002FScreenshot-2023-11-28-194443.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1286\" height=\"828\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F01\u002FScreenshot-2023-11-28-194443.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw1000\u002F2024\u002F01\u002FScreenshot-2023-11-28-194443.png 1000w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F01\u002FScreenshot-2023-11-28-194443.png 1286w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAn example of a malicious stream that was also preceded by a malicious ad\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhile the videos are clearly crafted with deep generative models, the support chats that the malicious websites use do not seem to employ any Large Language Model to answer.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"the-anatomy-of-youtube-account-takeovers\"\u003EThe anatomy of YouTube account takeovers\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThese account takeovers are usually enabled by the compromise of YouTube access tokens with the use of various stealers. After the access tokens are obtained, the malicious actors proceed with revamping the channel, making it look like it is owned by the entity they want to impersonate. This process is most likely automated and consists of completely changing the original channel by:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E Changing the channel name and handle – even though these are operations that can be done twice every 14 days, hackers manage to do it as it is uncommon for content creators to change names that often;\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EChanging the visibility of all videos to \u003Cstrong\u003Eprivate – \u003C\u002Fstrong\u003Ethis is done to conceal previously existing content as it can directly lead to the discovery of the scam;\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EChanging the channel avatar and banner – these are replaced with images that represent the impersonated entity;\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EChanging or eliminating the channel’s description, links, featured channels and anything that might lead to the identification of the original channel. In some instances, the channel link is set to the malicious website that promotes the crypto doubling scam.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn our research, we’ve observed some takeovers live. An example of this can be seen below.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe name, handle and avatar of the original channel were changed, but previously existing content is still available despite the 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EThe last wave of scams: MicroStrategy and the Bitcoin ETF\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ETaking advantage of the heavy news coverage of the Bitcoin ETF, malicious actors started broadcasting scams with the same topic in late December 2023. These scams have MicroStrategy (business intelligence company) and Michael Saylor as central figures, and use titles that refer to the Bitcoin ETF potentially reaching high values to gain traction. Hundreds of malicious broadcasts were observed in the last couple of weeks, qualifying it as one of the most intensive scam campaigns we’ve seen so far.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F01\u002Fsaylor_campaign.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EMost of the broadcasts use looped deep fakes in which MicroStrategy’s former CEO encourages the community to “participate in the giveaway” by scanning the QR code and following the instructions found on the website.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe compromised channels use variations of the official MicroStrategy logo as the avatar and the official banner, and some refer to the playlists of the official MicroStrategy channel to boost credibility. The thumbnails of the videos are also common between instances, with limited diversity. The most common name after the takeover is \u003Cstrong\u003EMicroStrategy US\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E and other discovered names are: MicroStrategy, Microstrategy, Microstrategy US, Microstrategy Live, Micro Strategy. The names might include trailing spaces and parentheses (rounded or square) around the \u003Cstrong\u003EUS \u003C\u002Fstrong\u003Eand \u003Cstrong\u003ELive\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E keywords.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F01\u002FPicture7.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"336\" height=\"59\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe phony websites are usually hosted on domains that resemble the name of the impersonated company or its former CEO, or simpler domains that include the symbols of the cryptocurrencies used in the fake giveaways, along with multipliers such as \u003Cem\u003E2x \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eor \u003Cem\u003Ex2\u003C\u002Fem\u003E. These websites also host animations that give users the impression that multiple transactions are taking place live. While it may seem legitimate, these are in fact randomly generated.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F01\u002FPicture6-1.png 640w\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHere are some key insights about what the deepfake Michael Saylor tells viewers in the looped video:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E-       You don’t need to register on any website. You need to watch the live broadcast online, keep an eye out for the QR code that will appear on the screen and scan it with your phone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E-       You don’t need to register on the website to make a Bitcoin deposit. Once you’ve accessed the platform, you’ll be prompted to deposit any amount of Bitcoin.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E-       After you deposit, our system will automatically send back double the amount of Bitcoin you deposited.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E-       We’ve ensured that the entire process is smooth and hassle-free to those who are new to the world of cryptocurrencies.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E-       Our technical support team will be available during the broadcast to assist with any queries or guidance\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E-       Unlike traditional giveaways that rely on chance, our mode is based on a guaranteed outcome. When participants deposit Bitcoin, they automatically receive double.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E-       The sooner you participate, the better your chance is, as the offer is time sensitive and depends on the availability of the funds allocated for the giveaway.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EUpdated numbers on the phenomenon\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E·      Maximum number of subscribers of a hijacked account: ~12,500,000 (for one account)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E·      Maximum number of views of a hijacked account:  ~3,869,224,308 (total views\u002Fone channel)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E·      Subscribers count median value: ~3955\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E·      View count of channel median value: ~449,159\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E·      Total number of subscribers from the top 10 hijacked channels: ~62,930,000\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E·      Total number of views from the most viewed 10 hijacked channels: ~17,447,370,155\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E·      According to our analysis, cybercriminals targeted a variety of content creator accounts, including the US (96 accounts), Brazil (75 accounts), India (74 accounts), Indonesia (49 accounts), Mexico (21 accounts), Turkey (15 accounts), Peru (14 accounts), Vietnam (13 accounts), Columbia (12 accounts), the UK (11 accounts), France (9 accounts), Spain (8 accounts, and much more. The number of compromised accounts does not include any accounts already banned by YouTube following malicious\u002Ffraudulent broadcasts\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAll metrics have grown since our last \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bitdefender.com\u002Fblog\u002Flabs\u002Fa-deep-dive-into-stream-jacking-attacks-on-youtube-and-why-theyre-so-popular\u002F\"\u003Ereport\u003C\u002Fa\u003E on the topic, while some even come close to doubling. The alarming growth indicates that this phenomenon is far from eradicated.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ETop 10 most subscribed hijacked channels\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-begin: html--\u003E\u003Ctable class=\"MsoTableGrid\" border=\"1\" cellspacing=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" style=\"caret-color: rgb(0, 0, 0); As such, we began an investigation of a subset of malicious domains (focusing on the latest trends – XRP, MicroStrategy, SpaceX and Binance) that were promoted in livestreams to get an idea of the actual “profits.” After extracting the identifiers of the promoted crypto wallets, the associated transactions were analyzed, with the following insights:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E·      Over 10 ETH (Ethereum, having a value per coin between ~$2180 and ~$2690 since January 1,\u003Csup\u003E,\u003C\u002Fsup\u003E2024) and 12 BTC (Bitcoin, having a value per coin between ~$42,200 and ~$48,700 since January 1, 2024) were sent to the malicious wallets;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E·      Most of the wallets had no transactions. This can also be related to the fact that their date of creation is quite recent, so it is likely that the numbers will grow in the future;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E·      Hackers use well-known measures of passing the tokens through a series of other wallets to complicate future analyses;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E·      The highest amounts received are almost 6 BTC and 2 ETH.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn total, potential earnings amount to ~$528,200 and ~$600,500 (depending on what date the coins are evaluated), making these malicious operations highly profitable for threat actors. While the analysis solely relies on the transactions received, it is unclear if these transactions are from the actual victims or transactions from other wallets used in this kind of scam. Nonetheless, the numbers are alarming, and the need to raise awareness of such frauds is paramount.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EFighting fire with fire. Minecraft Mods Lead to Multi-Stage, Multi-Platform Infostealer Malware",slug:"infected-minecraft-mods-lead-to-multi-stage-multi-platform-infostealer-malware",feature_image:"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2023\u002F06\u002Fminecraft-1106252_1920.jpg",featured:e,published_at:"2023-06-08T20:00:00.000+03:00",custom_excerpt:a,html:"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EJune 9 Update:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe oldest sample we were able to track until now (\u003Ccode\u003Ee69b50d1d58056fc770c88c514af9a82\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) shows the malware during its early development stage. Dated 2023-04-12, it looks like a Stage 2 sample with the C&amp;C address set to \u003Ccode\u003E127.0.0.1\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, which leads us to believe that it was used for testing. It also includes limited functionality that currently is available in Stage 3 samples (only listening for OS commands (executed with  \u003Ccode\u003Eexec\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) ), which reinforces our assumption that the malware was in development at that time.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe also noticed that the Java package was named differently back in April ( \u003Ccode\u003Edev.sirlennox.nekoclient\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E  instead of  \u003Ccode\u003Edev.neko.nekoclient\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E). \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe also identified several executables (NekoInstaller\u002FNekoService), as described below:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003ENekoInstaller contains a Portable Executable file named NekoServices; at execution it drops the executable file in  \u003Ccode\u003EC:\\Program Files\\nekoservice\\ServiceHost.exe\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E  and adds it as a service named  \u003Ccode\u003ENekoService\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E  to run;\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ENekoService contains a JAR file as a resource; it will download a JRE and run the JAR file; the JAR file is then dropped in  \u003Ccode\u003EC:\\Program Files\\nekoservice\\service.jar\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003Ethe JAR file seems to be a Stage 2 sample\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003Ethe MZ header compilation time for most of these samples ranges between 2023-04-20 18:20:06 and 2023-05-01 22:17:25, and just one sample was identified to be compiled on 2023-05-21 07:58:12, which means that the malware was in development in that timeframe.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EBased on this evidence, it seems that the attackers initially planned to distribute EXE files rather than JAR ones, but we were unable to assess whether the EXE files have been disseminated in the wild or not.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003EInitial article:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESeveral Minecraft mods and plugins hosted on the CurseForge and Bukkit modding communities \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bitdefender.com\u002Fblog\u002Fhotforsecurity\u002Ffractureiser-malware-discovered-in-minecraft-mods-spreading-uncertainty\u002F\"\u003Ehave been tainted\u003C\u002Fa\u003E with a multi-stage, multi-platform infostealer malware called Fractureiser, a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgithub.com\u002Ffractureiser-investigation\u002Ffractureiser\u002Fblob\u002Fmain\u002Fdocs\u002Ftech.md\"\u003Epreliminary investigation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E shows.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESeveral CurseForge and Bukkit accounts have been compromised and used to publish malware-rigged updates of mods and plugins without the knowledge of the original author. These mods have trickled downstream into popular modpacks that have been downloaded several million times to date.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe malware has 4 stages, labeled 0 through 3. Stage 0 is considered the modified mod or plugin to include obfuscated code that connects to \u003Ccode\u003Ehttp:\u002F\u002F85.217.144.130:8080\u002Fdl\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E to download the Stage 1 malware.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe Stage 1 malware comes in the form of a dl.jar file with a SHA-1 sum of \u003Ccode\u003Edc43c4685c3f47808ac207d1667cc1eb915b2d82\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. The Stage 1 malware includes a mutex to prevent it from running multiple times, and it seems responsible for infecting other JAR files, establishing persistence and contacting the command and control server in preparation of Stage 2 deployment.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EStage 2 (lib.jar or libWebGL64.jar) acts as a downloader and updater for the final payload in Stage 3.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EStage 3 brings the final payload, in the form of a jar file that includes a native binary named hook.dll. Hook.dll is exposing two functionalities that are called from Java code: \u003Ccode\u003EretrieveClipboardFiles\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E - to retrieve file descriptors from the clipboard, used for the virtual machine escape technique (detailed below), as well as \u003Ccode\u003EretrieveMSACredentials\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E to retrieve Microsoft Live credentials.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"what-we-know-so-far\"\u003EWhat we know so far\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe first sample apparently dates all the way back to April 24th 2023 in the form of a Stage 0 malware with the \u003Ccode\u003E0e583c572ad823330b9e34d871fcc2df\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E hash. The first JAR (Java Archive) file lacks many of the features currently in the malware.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe malware currently affects Linux and Windows Minecraft installs and attempts to inject itself into all other eligible .jar files on the system, including those that are not part of a Minecraft mod. The malware has a complex logic to determine whether a .jar file is a candidate for infection. Upon modification of the file, the infection code also disables code signing for Java files by removing the \u003Ccode\u003EMETA-INF\u002FCERTIFIC.RSA\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, \u003Ccode\u003EMETA-INF\u002FCERTIFIC.EC\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, \u003Ccode\u003EMETA-INF\u002FCERT.SF\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and \u003Ccode\u003EMETA-INF\u002FCERTIFIC.SF\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe malware monitors the clipboard for crypto-currency wallet addresses, then swaps them with the attacker’s to hijack transactions. It also steals Minecraft and Discord authentication tokens, as well as cookies and login data stored in the most popular browsers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EDuring our analysis, we identified interesting behavior we believe is aimed at mod or plugin developers. It looks like the Stage 3 malware targets Windows Sandbox instances used for testing mods by monitoring and constantly poisoning the clipboard in an attempt to infect the host. This behavior is isolated to Windows Sandbox, as it is the only virtualization environment that allows alteration of the host clipboard contents when the virtual machine is running in the background.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe were able to confirm that dozens of mods and plugins have been rigged with the malware. The affected mods are listed in the Indicators of Compromise section below.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe overwhelming majority of victims are in the US. We are monitoring the individual components of this malware and will update the threat distribution accordingly.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"mitigation\"\u003EMitigation\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBitdefender identifies the malicious code in all stages of execution as \u003Ccode\u003ETrojan.Java.Fractureiser.*\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. 9 Update:\n\nThe oldest sample we were able to track until now (e69b50d1d58056fc770c88c514af9a82) shows the malware during its early development stage. Dated 2023-04-12, it looks like a Stage 2 sample with the C&C address set to 127.0.0.1, which leads us to believe that it was used for testing. It also includes limited functionality that currently is available in Stage 3 samples (only listening for OS commands (executed with  exec) ), which reinforces our assumption that the malware was in de",reading_time:5,url:"\u002Fblog\u002Flabs\u002Finfected-minecraft-mods-lead-to-multi-stage-multi-platform-infostealer-malware\u002F"},{id:"66d5c3d2d0ec1aefc7d722b9",title:"Vulnerabilities identified in\nAmazon Fire TV Stick, Insignia\nFireOS TV Series",slug:"vulnerabilities-identified-amazon-fire-tv-stick-insignia-fire-os-tv-series",feature_image:"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2023\u002F05\u002Fold-tv-gab6450206_1920.png",featured:e,published_at:"2023-05-02T16:00:00.000+03:00",custom_excerpt:a,html:"\u003Cp\u003EStreaming devices have become increasingly popular in recent years, and for good reason. Portable, frequently updated and relatively inexpensive when compared to a new smart TV, these devices offer a convenient, cost-effective, and customizable way to access a vast selection of content from the comfort of your own home. Smart TVs and streaming devices account for \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bitdefender.com\u002Fblog\u002Fhotforsecurity\u002Fa-smart-device-in-your-home-is-extremely-unsafe-iot-report-finds\u002F\"\u003Ea whopping 20%\u003C\u002Fa\u003E [pdf] of all connected IoT devices, and potential vulnerabilities in firmware could affect a significant user base.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAs the creator of the world’s first smart home cybersecurity hub, Bitdefender regularly audits popular IoT hardware for vulnerabilities that might affect customers if left unaddressed. This research paper is part of a broader program and aims to shed light on the security of the world’s best-sellers in the IoT space. This report covers the Amazon Fire TV Stick and the Insignia\u003Cbr\u003EFireOS TV products. The research discloses vulnerabilities affecting the following products and versions:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EInsignia TV with FireOS versions before \u003Ccode\u003E6.2.9.5\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EFire TV Stick 3rd gen. with FireOS versions before \u003Ccode\u003E7.6.3.3\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ENote: the vulnerabilities presented in this report have been responsibly disclosed to the vendor through their Bug Bounty program. Amazon has released fixes for these issues on Fire TV devices and the Fire TV remote app, and the company has no evidence that this issue has been used against customers. Bitdefender has been working closely with the Amazon Fire TV team through all stages of vulnerability disclosure. We would like to extend our thanks for the prompt response time, communication, transparency and escalation.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"vulnerabilities-at-a-glance\"\u003EVulnerabilities at a glance\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EUnauthorized authentication through local network PIN brute forcing. This vulnerability was caused by improper implementation of the Password Authenticated Key Exchange by Juggling (or J-PAKE) protocol that could have resulted in attackers gaining control of the device. (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fcve.mitre.org\u002Fcgi-bin\u002Fcvename.cgi?name=CVE-2023-1385\"\u003ECVE-2023-1385\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EA vulnerability in the setMediaSource function on the amzn.thin.pl service allowed for arbitrary Javascript code to be executed. It could be used to load arbitrary HTTP URLs in the webview. (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fcve.mitre.org\u002Fcgi-bin\u002Fcvename.cgi?name=CVE-2023-1384\"\u003ECVE-2023-1384\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EA vulnerability in the exchangeDeviceServices function on the amzn.dmgr service allowed an attacker to register services that are only locally accessible.
